			var oldonload = window.onload;

	<header class="article-header">
		
		<section class="tags ">
			<a class="brand-tag brand-time-tag" href="http://time.com/">TIME</a>
			
				<a class="section-tag" itemprop="articleSection" href="http://time.com/ideas/" data-event="section-ideas">Ideas</a>
				<a class="topic-tag" itemprop="articleSection" href="http://time.com/tag/religion/" data-event="tag-religion" >Religion</a>
		</section>


		<h2 class="article-title" itemprop="headline">Pope Francis&#8217; Guide to Lent: What You Should Give Up This Year</h2>

	<div class="article-sub-headline">
		<div class="article-meta">
						<ul class="article-authors">
								<li class="article-author ">
									<span class="byline"><a itemprop="author" href="http://time.com/author/christopher-j-hale-2/">Christopher J. Hale</a></span>
									<a class="author-twitter" target="_blank" href="https://twitter.com/chrisjollyhale">@chrisjollyhale</a>
								</li>
						</ul>

			<time class="publish-date" itemprop="datePublished" datetime="2015-02-18 16:55:23" pubdate>Feb. 18, 2015</time>
			
			
		</div>
		<div class="social-links">
			<a class="expand-share" href="javascript:void 0;" title="Click to view article share options">SHARE</a>
		<span class="social-links-tooltip">

		</div>
	</div>	</header>	<section class="article-body article-collapse-body" itemprop="articleBody">
			
				<figure class="article-hero landscape">
					<div class="article-hero_wrapper">
						<img src="https://timedotcom.files.wordpress.com/2015/02/pope-francis3.jpg?quality=75&amp;strip=color&amp;w=550" itemprop="image" alt="Pope Francis leads the Ash Wednesday mass , Feb.18, 2015 at Santa Sabina church in Rome." data-srcset="https://timedotcom.files.wordpress.com/2015/02/pope-francis3.jpg?quality=75&amp;strip=color&amp;w=1100 800w, https://timedotcom.files.wordpress.com/2015/02/pope-francis3.jpg?quality=75&amp;strip=color&amp;w=1100 800w 2x"/>
						<div class="hero-image-buttons">
							<a class="time-icons time-icons-pinterest social-link-pinterest popup" href="https://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http%3A%2F%2Ftime.com%2F3714056%2Fpope-francis-lent-2015-fasting%2F&media=https://timedotcom.files.wordpress.com/2015/02/pope-francis3.jpg?quality=75&strip=color&w=550&description=Pope+Francis%E2%80%99+Guide+to+Lent%3A+What+You+Should+Give+Up+This+Year" data-event="pinterest" title="Click to pin this article to Pinterest"></a>
						</div>
					</div>
					<figcaption class="image-caption">
						<span class="credit">Gabriel Bouys—AFP/Getty Images</span>
						<span class="caption">Pope Francis leads the Ash Wednesday mass on Feb. 18, 2015 in Rome. </span>
					</figcaption>
				</figure>
			<p class="contributor-authors">
				<span class="time-icons time-icons-ideas"></span><span>Christopher Hale is executive director at Catholics in Alliance for the Common Good and the co-founder of Millennial.</span>
				
			</p>
			<h2 class="article-excerpt" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">No need to throw out the chocolate, booze, and carbs. Pope Francis has a different idea for fasting this year.</h2>
			<div class="clipper-content">
				<p>Christians around the world mark the beginning of Lent with the celebration of Ash Wednesday. This ancient day and season has a surprising modern appeal. Priests and pastors often tell you that outside of Christmas, more people show up to church on Ash Wednesday than any other day of the year&mdash;including Easter. But this mystique isn&#8217;t reserved for Christians alone. The customs that surround the season have a quality to them that transcend religion.</p>
<p>Perhaps most notable is the act of fasting. While Catholics fast on Ash Wednesday and on Fridays during the Lenten season, many people&mdash;religious or not&mdash;take up <a style="background-color:initial;" href="http://www.bbc.com/news/magazine-25549805" target="_blank">this increasingly popular discipline</a> during the year.</p>
<p><strong>MORE </strong><a href="http://time.com/3713500/lenten-fast-twitter-ash-wednesday/" target="_blank">Here&rsquo;s What People On Twitter Say They&rsquo;re Giving Up For Lent</a></p>
<p>But Pope Francis has asked us to reconsider the heart of this activity this Lenten season. According to Francis, fasting must never become superficial. <a href="http://www.zenit.org/en/articles/cardinal-bergoglio-s-lenten-message-for-buenos-aires" target="_blank">He often quotes the early Christian mystic John Chrysostom</a> who said: &#8220;No act of virtue can be great if it is not followed by advantage for others. So, no matter how much time you spend fasting, no matter how much you sleep on a hard floor and eat ashes and sigh continually, if you do no good to others, you do nothing great.&#8221;</p>
<p>But this isn&#8217;t to downplay the role of sacrifice during the Lenten season. Lent is a good time for penance and self-denial. But once again, <a href="http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/messages/lent/documents/papa-francesco_20131226_messaggio-quaresima2014.html" target="_blank">Francis reminds us that these activities must truly enrich others</a>: &#8220;I distrust a charity that costs nothing and does not hurt.&#8221;</p>
<div class="article-video"><div class="video-wrapper brightcove-size-large" data-pos="1" data-continuous="1" data-playlist="0"><object id="bc-video-2916220526001-1" class="BrightcoveExperience"><param name="bgcolor" value="#000000"><param name="width" value="100%"><param name="height" value="100%"><param name="playerID" value="1847503743001"><param name="isVid" value="true"><param name="isUI" value="true"><param name="dynamicStreaming" value="true"><param name="videoSmoothing" value="true"><param name="linkBaseURL" value="http://ti.me/1LhpC1Z"><param name="includeAPI" value="true"><param name="templateLoadHandler" value="Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad"><param name="templateReadyHandler" value="Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady"><param name="wmode" value="opaque"><param name="htmlFallback" value="true"><param name="@videoPlayer" value="2916220526001"></object></div></div>
<p>So, if we&#8217;re going to fast from anything this Lent, Francis suggests that even more than candy or alcohol, we fast from indifference towards others.</p>
<p>In his annual Lenten message, <a href="http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/messages/lent/documents/papa-francesco_20141004_messaggio-quaresima2015.html" target="_blank">the pope writes</a>, &#8220;Indifference to our neighbor and to God also represents a real temptation for us Christians. Each year during Lent we need to hear once more the voice of the prophets who cry out and trouble our conscience.&#8221;</p><div class="content-ad" id="content-ad-3714056"></div>
<p>Describing this phenomenon he calls the <em>globalization of indifference</em>, <a href="http://w2.vatican.va/content/francesco/en/apost_exhortations/documents/papa-francesco_esortazione-ap_20131124_evangelii-gaudium.html" target="_blank">Francis writes</a> that &#8220;whenever our interior life becomes caught up in its own interests and concerns, there is no longer room for others, no place for the poor. God&#8217;s voice is no longer heard, the quiet joy of his love is no longer felt, and the desire to do good fades.&#8221; He continues that, &#8220;We end up being incapable of feeling compassion at the outcry of the poor, weeping for other people&#8217;s pain, and feeling a need to help them, as though all this were someone else&#8217;s responsibility and not our own.&#8221;</p>
<p><b>MORE </b><a href="http://time.com/3710419/pope-new-cardinals/" target="_blank">Pope to New Cardinals: Practice Compassion, Be Open to All</a></p>
<p>But when we fast from this indifference, we can began to feast on love. In fact, Lent is the perfect time to learn how to love again. Jesus&mdash;the great protagonist of this holy season&mdash;certainly showed us the way. In him, God descends all the way down to bring everyone up. In his life and his ministry, no one is excluded.</p>
<p>&#8220;What are you giving up for Lent?&#8221; It&#8217;s a question a lot of people will get these next few days. If you want to change your body, perhaps alcohol and candy is the way to go. But if you want to change your heart, a harder fast is needed. This narrow road is gritty, but it isn&#8217;t sterile. It will make room in ourselves to experience a love that can make us whole and set us free.</p>
<p>Now that&#8217;s something worth fasting for.</p>
<p><em>Read next: <a href="http://time.com/3713126/ash-wednesday/?xid=time_readnext" target="_blank">3 Things to Know About Ash Wednesday</a></em></p>

He helped lead national Catholic outreach for President Barack Obama's 2012 re-election campaign.","short_bio":"Christopher Hale is executive director at Catholics in Alliance for the Common Good and the co-founder of Millennial.","types":["skyword"],"twitter":"chrisjollyhale","twitter_url":"https:\/\/twitter.com\/chrisjollyhale","gplus":"","fb":"","email":"","thumbnail":null,"contributor":true,"search_link":"http:\/\/search.time.com\/results.html?Ntt=Christopher+J.+Hale"}],"has_authors":true,"content":"<p>Christians around the world mark the beginning of Lent with the celebration of Ash Wednesday. This ancient day and season has a surprising modern appeal. Priests and pastors often tell you that outside of Christmas, more people show up to church on Ash Wednesday than any other day of the year&mdash;including Easter. But this mystique isn&#8217;t reserved for Christians alone. The customs that surround the season have a quality to them that transcend religion.<\/p>\n<p>Perhaps most notable is the act of fasting. While Catholics fast on Ash Wednesday and on Fridays during the Lenten season, many people&mdash;religious or not&mdash;take up <a style=\"background-color:initial;\" href=\"http:\/\/www.bbc.com\/news\/magazine-25549805\" target=\"_blank\">this increasingly popular discipline<\/a> during the year.<\/p>\n<p><strong>MORE <\/strong><a href=\"http:\/\/time.com\/3713500\/lenten-fast-twitter-ash-wednesday\/\" target=\"_blank\">Here&rsquo;s What People On Twitter Say They&rsquo;re Giving Up For Lent<\/a><\/p>\n<p>But Pope Francis has asked us to reconsider the heart of this activity this Lenten season. According to Francis, fasting must never become superficial. <a href=\"http:\/\/www.zenit.org\/en\/articles\/cardinal-bergoglio-s-lenten-message-for-buenos-aires\" target=\"_blank\">He often quotes the early Christian mystic John Chrysostom<\/a> who said: &#8220;No act of virtue can be great if it is not followed by advantage for others. So, no matter how much time you spend fasting, no matter how much you sleep on a hard floor and eat ashes and sigh continually, if you do no good to others, you do nothing great.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>But this isn&#8217;t to downplay the role of sacrifice during the Lenten season. Lent is a good time for penance and self-denial. But once again, <a href=\"http:\/\/w2.vatican.va\/content\/francesco\/en\/messages\/lent\/documents\/papa-francesco_20131226_messaggio-quaresima2014.html\" target=\"_blank\">Francis reminds us that these activities must truly enrich others<\/a>: &#8220;I distrust a charity that costs nothing and does not hurt.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper brightcove-size-large\" data-pos=\"3\" data-continuous=\"1\" data-playlist=\"0\"><object id=\"bc-video-2916220526001-3\" class=\"BrightcoveExperience\"><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#000000\"><param name=\"width\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"height\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"playerID\" value=\"1847503743001\"><param name=\"isVid\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"isUI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"dynamicStreaming\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"videoSmoothing\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"linkBaseURL\" value=\"http:\/\/ti.me\/1LhpC1Z\"><param name=\"includeAPI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"templateLoadHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad\"><param name=\"templateReadyHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady\"><param name=\"wmode\" value=\"opaque\"><param name=\"htmlFallback\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"@videoPlayer\" value=\"2916220526001\"><\/object><\/div><\/div>\n<p>So, if we&#8217;re going to fast from anything this Lent, Francis suggests that even more than candy or alcohol, we fast from indifference towards others.<\/p>\n<p>In his annual Lenten message, <a href=\"http:\/\/w2.vatican.va\/content\/francesco\/en\/messages\/lent\/documents\/papa-francesco_20141004_messaggio-quaresima2015.html\" target=\"_blank\">the pope writes<\/a>, &#8220;Indifference to our neighbor and to God also represents a real temptation for us Christians. Each year during Lent we need to hear once more the voice of the prophets who cry out and trouble our conscience.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"content-ad\" id=\"content-ad-3714056\"><\/div>\n<p>Describing this phenomenon he calls the <em>globalization of indifference<\/em>, <a href=\"http:\/\/w2.vatican.va\/content\/francesco\/en\/apost_exhortations\/documents\/papa-francesco_esortazione-ap_20131124_evangelii-gaudium.html\" target=\"_blank\">Francis writes<\/a> that &#8220;whenever our interior life becomes caught up in its own interests and concerns, there is no longer room for others, no place for the poor. God&#8217;s voice is no longer heard, the quiet joy of his love is no longer felt, and the desire to do good fades.&#8221; He continues that, &#8220;We end up being incapable of feeling compassion at the outcry of the poor, weeping for other people&#8217;s pain, and feeling a need to help them, as though all this were someone else&#8217;s responsibility and not our own.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><b>MORE <\/b><a href=\"http:\/\/time.com\/3710419\/pope-new-cardinals\/\" target=\"_blank\">Pope to New Cardinals: Practice Compassion, Be Open to All<\/a><\/p>\n<p>But when we fast from this indifference, we can began to feast on love. In fact, Lent is the perfect time to learn how to love again. Jesus&mdash;the great protagonist of this holy season&mdash;certainly showed us the way. In him, God descends all the way down to bring everyone up. In his life and his ministry, no one is excluded.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;What are you giving up for Lent?&#8221; It&#8217;s a question a lot of people will get these next few days. If you want to change your body, perhaps alcohol and candy is the way to go. But if you want to change your heart, a harder fast is needed. This narrow road is gritty, but it isn&#8217;t sterile. It will make room in ourselves to experience a love that can make us whole and set us free.<\/p>\n<p>Now that&#8217;s something worth fasting for.<\/p>\n<p><em>Read next: <a href=\"http:\/\/time.com\/3713126\/ash-wednesday\/?xid=time_readnext\" target=\"_blank\">3 Things to Know About Ash Wednesday<\/a><\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"galleryContainer Pope Francis has a different idea for fasting this year.","canonical_link":""}},"topic":{"success":{"name":"Success","tax":"topic","left_rail_title":"All Success Content","left_rail_subhead":"More Success Content","topic_header_title":"Success","articles":[{"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/4152490\/become-successful\/","shortlink":"http:\/\/ti.me\/1UAQcHE","title":"How to Stop Being Jealous of Successful People","friendly_title":"How to Stop Being Jealous of Successful People","post_type":"post","available":true,"time_article":true,"comments_allowed":true,"sub_learn_more_url":"https:\/\/subscription.time.com\/storefront\/subscribe-to-time\/link\/1032487.html","show_comments":true,"short_title":"How to Stop Being Jealous of Successful People","contributor":true,"excerpt":"Become one","format":"article","time":{"pretty":"Dec. 29, 2015","published":"2015-12-29 12:00:11","updated":"2015-12-29 17:00:11","minute":"12:00 pm","short":"12\/29"},"authors":[{"id":290078355,"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/author\/entrepreneur-2\/","name":"Daniel DiPiazza \/ Entrepreneur","bio":"","short_bio":"","types":["contributor"],"twitter":"","twitter_url":"","gplus":"","fb":"","email":"","thumbnail":null,"contributor":true,"search_link":false}],"has_authors":true,"content":"<p>How many times have you caught yourself clicking through the Facebook profile pictures of a &ldquo;friend&rdquo; (whom you&rsquo;ve never met) at 1:37 a.m., and getting at least a <em>teeny<\/em> bit jealous because they seem to be living a much more exciting life than you, full of better looking people and more money?<\/p>\n<p>And they&#8217;re always on vacation. Dear God! Why are all their pictures from vacations?<\/p>\n<p>Who&rsquo;s giving out these cruises?<\/p>\n<p>Seeing this type of stuff used to bother me for three reasons:<\/p>\n<p>First, I felt like I was &ldquo;behind&rdquo; for my age. At 24, I had close friends who were moving up the corporate ladder quickly and making what I thought was big money. Other friends were doing really cool, exciting work getting doctorates or professional degrees.<\/p>\n<p>I didn&rsquo;t want either of those, but I couldn&rsquo;t help feeling like a dweeb talking to them sometimes &mdash; <a href=\"http:\/\/www.rich20something.com\/posted-this-on-my-facebook-page-tonight-thought-id-share\/\" target=\"_blank\">I even vented about it in an open letter.<\/a><\/p>\n<p>When they asked me what I was doing, all I could really tell them was that I was still working at a restaurant and trying to &#8220;figure things out.&rdquo;<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\">Second, I felt like nobody had my back. I knew I wanted to start my own business(es), but I didn&rsquo;t have any mentors to give me solid advice or a step-by-step action plan. I didn&rsquo;t have anybody close to me who knew the ropes and could help me if I fell down. I wanted someone to tell me &ldquo;do this, then do that.&rdquo;<\/p>\n<p>Unlike the corporate world or graduate school, there are really no guidelines or &ldquo;best practices&rdquo; for entrepreneurship. You pretty much have to figure it out yourself. That&rsquo;s why it&rsquo;s so scary.<\/p>\n<p>Third and last, I felt like I was in a vacuum. I was really the only person I knew in &ldquo;real life&rdquo; who wanted to be an entrepreneur. All the people at the places I worked at&hellip;they just wanted to clock in&hellip;.day after day.<\/p>\n<p>I wanted to meet other people like me. People who were driven to get more from their lives and really wanted to create something new.<\/p>\n<p>People I could bounce ideas off of and wouldn&rsquo;t make me feel &ldquo;weird&rdquo; for wanting to brainstorm or talk about personal development. I always knew that if I was able to fill my entire life with the type of people that I wanted to be like, success was pretty much guaranteed.<\/p><div class=\"content-ad\" id=\"content-ad-4152490\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper brightcove-size-large\" data-pos=\"5\" data-continuous=\"1\" data-playlist=\"0\"><object id=\"bc-video-4105230971001-5\" class=\"BrightcoveExperience\"><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#000000\"><param name=\"width\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"height\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"playerID\" value=\"1847503743001\"><param name=\"isVid\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"isUI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"dynamicStreaming\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"videoSmoothing\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"linkBaseURL\" value=\"http:\/\/ti.me\/1UAQcHE\"><param name=\"includeAPI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"templateLoadHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad\"><param name=\"templateReadyHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady\"><param name=\"wmode\" value=\"opaque\"><param name=\"htmlFallback\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"@videoPlayer\" value=\"4105230971001\"><\/object><\/div><\/div>\n<p>Here is how I got over the jealousy. For the past four years, I&rsquo;ve hustled to connect with other entrepreneurs who are doing amazing work. I&rsquo;ve gone out of my way to build mentorship relationships with startup founders, millionaires and high-performers in all fields.<\/p>\n<p>Why?<\/p>\n<p>Because I was sick of feeling jealous of people who are doing well. I realized that if I wanted to become one of them, I had to do whatever it took to get into their peer group.<\/p>\n<p>And I did. But It definitely didn&rsquo;t happen overnight. There&rsquo;s a process you have to learn when approaching successful people. (<a href=\"http:\/\/www.rich20something.com\/connect-anyone-ultimate-guide\/\" target=\"_blank\">Here&#8217;s the exact strategy I&#8217;ve used to develop authentic relationships with influencers.<\/a>) But I worked at it, and when I was finally able to cultivate a sizable community of super-high-value people around me, I noticed something incredible: it was almost impossible to fail.<\/p>\n<p>If I had a question, doubt or fear, there was an established community of people around me who actually <em>wanted <\/em>to help me. If I didn&rsquo;t know which way to turn, there was a mentor on speed dial for almost any problem I encountered.<\/p>\n<p>Above everything else, there was a new level of expectation put on me by those I had surrounded myself with. They just expected me to be doing well, and I didn&rsquo;t want to let them down. Turns out I had the makings of an entrepreneur in me all along.<\/p>\n<p>Building that community of friends and mentors was the ultimate tool to kick my progress into warp speed, and probably the biggest reason I was able to move from a day job to self-employment so quickly.<\/p>\n<p><em>This <a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/245917\">article<\/a> originally appeared on <a of Successful People","og_desc":"Become one","canonical_link":"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/245917\/"}},{"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/4137012\/success-peter-thiel\/","shortlink":"http:\/\/ti.me\/1Iud8H5","title":"4 Lessons for Success From the Cofounder of Paypal","friendly_title":"4 Lessons for Success From the Cofounder of Paypal","post_type":"post","available":true,"time_article":true,"comments_allowed":true,"sub_learn_more_url":"https:\/\/subscription.time.com\/storefront\/subscribe-to-time\/link\/1032487.html","show_comments":true,"short_title":"4 Lessons for Success From the Cofounder of Paypal","contributor":true,"excerpt":"Stay open-minded and flexible","format":"article","time":{"pretty":"Dec. 8, 2015","published":"2015-12-08 00:01:08","updated":"2015-12-08 05:01:08","minute":"12:01 am","short":"12\/8"},"authors":[{"id":52736297,"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/author\/shane-parrish\/","name":"Shane Parrish","bio":"","short_bio":"Shane Parrish writes Farnam Street","types":["contributor"],"twitter":"farnamstreet","twitter_url":"https:\/\/twitter.com\/farnamstreet","gplus":"","fb":"","email":"","thumbnail":null,"contributor":true,"search_link":false}],"has_authors":true,"content":"<p>The <a href=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/2015\/11\/the-single-best-interview-question-you-can-ask\/\">best interview question<\/a> &mdash; what important truth do very few people agree with you on?&mdash; is tough to answer. Just think about it for a second.<\/p>\n<p>In his book <em><a class=\"external\" href=\"http:\/\/www.amazon.com\/gp\/product\/0804139296\/?tag=timecom-20\" rel=\"nofollow\">Zero to One<\/a><\/em>, Peter Thiel argues that it might be easier to start with what everyone seems to agree on and go until you disagree.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>If you can identify a delusional popular belief, you can find what lies hidden behind it: the contrarian truth.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Consider the proposition that companies should make money for their shareholders and not lose it. This seems self-evident, but it wasn&rsquo;t so obvious to many in the late 90s. Remember back then? No loss was too big. (In my <a href=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/2015\/09\/sanjay-bakshireading-mental-models-worldly-wisdom\/\">interview with Sanjay Bakshi<\/a> he suggested that to some extent this still exists today.)<\/p>\n<p>Making money? That was old school. In the late 1990s it was all about the new economy. Eyeballs first, profits later.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>Conventional beliefs only ever come to appear arbitrary and wrong in retrospect; whenever one collapses, we call the old belief a bubble. But the distortions caused by bubbles don&rsquo;t disappear when they pop. The internet craze of the &rsquo;90s was the biggest bubble since the crash of 1929, and the lessons learned afterward define and distort almost all thinking about technology today. The first step to thinking clearly is to question what we think we know about the past.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>There&rsquo;s really no need to rehash the 1990s in this article. You can google it. Or you can read the summary in chapter two of <em><a class=\"external\" href=\"http:\/\/www.amazon.com\/gp\/product\/0804139296\/?tag=timecom-20\" rel=\"nofollow\">Zero to One<\/a><\/em>.<\/p>\n<p>Where things get interesting, at least in the thinking context, are the lessons we drew from the late 90s. Thiel says the following were lessons most commonly learned:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>The entrepreneurs who stuck with Silicon Valley learned four big lessons from the dot-com crash that still guide business thinking today:<\/p>\n<p><strong>1. Make incremental advances.<\/strong> Grand visions inflated the bubble, so they should not be indulged. Anyone who claims to be able to do something great is suspect, and anyone who wants to change the world should be more humble. Small, incremental steps are the only safe path forward.<\/p>\n<p><strong>2. Stay lean and flexible.<\/strong> All companies must be &ldquo;lean,&rdquo; which is code for &ldquo;unplanned.&rdquo; You should not know what your business will do; planning is arrogant and inflexible. Instead you should try things out, &ldquo;iterate,&rdquo; and treat entrepreneurship as agnostic experimentation.<\/p>\n<p><strong>3. Improve on the competition.<\/strong> Don&rsquo;t try to create a new market prematurely. The only way to know you have a real business is to start with an already existing customer, so you should build your company by improving on recognizable products already offered by successful competitors.<\/p>\n<p><strong>4. Focus on product, not sales.<\/strong> If your product requires advertising or salespeople to sell it, it&rsquo;s not good enough: technology is primarily about product development, not distribution. Bubble-era advertising was obviously wasteful, so the only sustainable growth is viral growth.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>These lessons, Thiel argues, are now <strong>dogma<\/strong> in the startup world. Ignore them at your peril and risk near certain failure. In fact, many private companies I&rsquo;ve worked with have adopted the same view. Governments too are attempting to replicate these &lsquo;facts&rsquo; &mdash; they have become conventional wisdom.<\/p>\n<p>And yet &hellip; the opposites are probably just as true if not more correct.<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>1. It is better to risk boldness than triviality.<br \/>\n2. A bad plan is better than no plan.<br \/>\n3. Competitive markets destroy profits.<br \/>\n4. Sales matters just as much as product.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>Such is the world of messy social science &mdash; hard and fast rules are difficult to come by, and frequently, good ideas lose value as they gain popularity. (This is the &ldquo;everyone on their tip-toes at a parade&rdquo; <a class=\"external\" href=\"http:\/\/www.berkshirehathaway.com\/letters\/1985.html\" rel=\"nofollow\">idea<\/a>.) Just as importantly, what starts as a good hand tends to be <em>overplayed<\/em> by <a href=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/mental-models\/\">man-with-a-hammer<\/a> types.<\/p>\n<p>And so the lessons which have been culled from the tech crash are not necessarily <em>wrong<\/em>, they are just <em>context-dependent<\/em>. It is hard to generalize with them.<\/p>\n<p>According to Thiel, we must learn to use our brains <em>as well as<\/em> our genitals:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>We still need new technology, and we may even need some 1999-style hubris and exuberance to get it. To build the next generation of companies, we must abandon the dogmas created after the crash. That doesn&rsquo;t mean the opposite ideas are automatically true: you can&rsquo;t escape the madness of crowds by dogmatically rejecting them. Instead ask yourself: how much of what you know about business is shaped by mistaken reactions to past mistakes? The most contrarian thing of all is not to oppose the crowd but to think for yourself.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>In a nutshell, when everyone learns the same lessons, applying them to the point of religious devotion, there can be opportunity in the opposite. If everyone is thinking the same thing, no one is really thinking.<\/p>\n<p>As Alfred Sloan, the heroic former CEO of General Motors, once put it:<\/p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-22761\" src=\"https:\/\/s0.wp.com\/wp-content\/themes\/vip\/plugins\/lazy-load\/images\/1x1.trans.gif\" data-lazy-src=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/11\/Alfred-Sloan.png\" alt=\"Alfred Sloan\" width=\"600\" \/><noscript><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-22761\" src=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/11\/Alfred-Sloan.png\" alt=\"Alfred Sloan\" width=\"600\" \/><\/noscript><\/p>\n<p class=\"clipper--hidden\"><em><strong>This piece originally appeared on <a href=\"https:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/2015\/12\/peter-thiel-end-of-hubris\/\" target=\"_blank\">Farnam Street<\/a>.<\/strong><\/em><\/p>\n<p class=\"clipper--hidden\"><strong>Join over 60,000 readers and get a free weekly update via email <a href=\"http:\/\/www.farnamstreetblog.com\/newsletter\/\" target=\"_blank\">here<\/a>.<\/strong><\/p>\n","read_more":true,"section":{"name":"Ideas","slug":"ideas","url":"http:\/\/time.com\/ideas\/","description":"TIME Ideas hosts the world's leading voices, providing commentary and expertise on the most compelling events in news, society, and culture. Is How Successful People Get Ahead During the Holidays","friendly_title":"This Is How Successful People Get Ahead During the Holidays","post_type":"post","available":true,"time_article":true,"comments_allowed":true,"sub_learn_more_url":"https:\/\/subscription.time.com\/storefront\/subscribe-to-time\/link\/1032487.html","show_comments":true,"short_title":"This Is How Successful People Get Ahead During the Holidays","contributor":true,"excerpt":"They live the '13-Month Year'","format":"article","time":{"pretty":"Dec. 7, 2015","published":"2015-12-07 17:33:22","updated":"2015-12-07 22:33:22","minute":"5:33 pm","short":"12\/7"},"authors":[{"id":290078355,"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/author\/entrepreneur-2\/","name":"Daniel DiPiazza \/ Entrepreneur","bio":"","short_bio":"","types":["contributor"],"twitter":"","twitter_url":"","gplus":"","fb":"","email":"","thumbnail":null,"contributor":true,"search_link":false}],"has_authors":true,"content":"<p>There&rsquo;s a disturbance in the Force. The weather is getting colder. Winter is setting in. The holiday season is soon upon us. I&rsquo;ve found that there are primarily two types of people that emerge when the holiday haze hits. Which one are you?<\/p>\n<p><strong>1. &ldquo;The Sheep&rdquo;<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>By Dec. 1, the Sheep are already mentally checked out. They might be here here physically, but their minds are roasting chestnuts over an open fire. &#8220;Dude&hellip;it&rsquo;s December,&rdquo; they&rsquo;ll tell you. The Sheep have plenty of big goals that they&rsquo;re hoping to accomplish in 2016. (I mean, who doesn&rsquo;t?) But right now, all that stuff is on the back burner. Going on mental cruise control around the holidays doesn&rsquo;t sound like such a bad idea for most people. I think we can all relate.<\/p>\n<p>But inevitably, a sinking feeling begins to develop. Right in your core.<\/p>\n<p>It starts very subtly, when you look back at 2015 goals and realize, &ldquo;Darn&hellip;I didn&rsquo;t really accomplish what I set out to do this year.&rdquo; <em>&ldquo;It&rsquo;s OK,&rdquo; <\/em>you tell yourself. <em>&ldquo;New Year, New Me. Right? I&rsquo;ll get a fresh start in January.&rdquo; <\/em>So you set new resolutions to get even <em>more<\/em> done in 2016. It feels good to envision yourself following through. Maybe you even write some things down.<\/p>\n<p>Deep down inside, though, you know nothing has really changed.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><span class=\"s1\"><div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper brightcove-size-large\" data-pos=\"9\" data-continuous=\"1\" data-playlist=\"0\"><object id=\"bc-video-4105230971001-9\" class=\"BrightcoveExperience\"><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#000000\"><param name=\"width\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"height\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"playerID\" value=\"1847503743001\"><param name=\"isVid\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"isUI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"dynamicStreaming\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"videoSmoothing\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"linkBaseURL\" value=\"http:\/\/ti.me\/1lcJdZP\"><param name=\"includeAPI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"templateLoadHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad\"><param name=\"templateReadyHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady\"><param name=\"wmode\" value=\"opaque\"><param name=\"htmlFallback\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"@videoPlayer\" value=\"4105230971001\"><\/object><\/div><\/div><\/span><\/p>\n<p>You don&rsquo;t really have a plan for getting from where you are to where you want to be, and in your heart-of-hearts&mdash;as much as it hurts you to admit it&mdash;you wouldn&rsquo;t exactly be surprised if December 2016 left you feeling just as unsatisfied as this year.<\/p>\n<p>So you just&hellip;bury your expectations in food and embrace the holiday slump. It&rsquo;s a nice six-ish weeks of self-induced, &ldquo;I&rsquo;ll deal with it after New Year&#8217;s&rdquo; bliss. But on a core level, it an agonizing cycle of self-defeat.<\/p>\n<p>That&rsquo;s how most of the population spends their holiday season. I&rsquo;ve been there, too. But there&rsquo;s another way.<\/p>\n<p><strong>2. &#8220;The Hustlers&rdquo;<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>On the outside, Hustlers seem like anomalies whose massive success can&rsquo;t be explained with logic. They&rsquo;re like &ldquo;glitches&rdquo; in the system. These are the people who set out to accomplish <em>massive<\/em> goals every single year, and not only <em>crush<\/em> those goals but surpass them.<\/p><div class=\"content-ad\" id=\"content-ad-4135795\"><\/div>\n<p>I know you&rsquo;ve seen them: Maybe you&rsquo;re reading <em>TIME<\/em> and catch a glimpse of some young, brilliant entrepreneur in his 20s who&rsquo;s making billions with an app he developed in his dorm room. Or perhaps it&rsquo;s the newest junior executive at your job, who despite being with the company for less time than you, has already put herself on track to become a partner.<\/p>\n<p>How are they doing it?<\/p>\n<p>The 13-Month Year is how true Hustlers get ahead. More than anything, someone living a 13-Month Year says: <em>&ldquo;I don&rsquo;t care that everyone else is taking the holidays off. I&rsquo;m about to turn the rocket boosters ON.&rdquo;<\/em><\/p>\n<p>While your friends and colleagues are winding down, eating a lot and singing carols, they&#8217;re grinding through the holidays. They&#8217;re starting their year early and they get an entire &ldquo;bonus&rdquo; month in 2016 to figure things out without wasting time. They&#8217;re working out all the kinks in your plans so that come Jan. 1, while everyone else is sobering up and crawling back to the office, they&#8217;re already well into the groove.<\/p>\n<p>THAT&rsquo;S how winners kill the game.<\/p>\n<p>This isn&rsquo;t another played out New Year&rsquo;s Resolution that you&#8217;ll sweep under the rug in a few weeks, quietly embarrassed. This is a proven strategy for success. If you want to get in better shape, maybe you&rsquo;ll use that extra month to start your workout routine and diet plan early. (You&rsquo;d be appalled how empty the gym is in December. Only Hustlers are gettin&rsquo; it in. Perfect.) <a href=\"http:\/\/rich20something.com\/\" target=\"_blank\">If you want to start a business<\/a>, maybe that extra month is used to begin testing your ideas early and identify where to focus your efforts so that you already have momentum and clarity going into 2016.<\/p>\n<p>Now here&rsquo;s the catch&#8230;. This stuff is not easy.<\/p>\n<p>I&rsquo;m not a guru. I&rsquo;m just <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/c\/Rich20Something?sub_confirmation=1\">Daniel<\/a>. I&rsquo;m not a millionaire (yet). I&rsquo;m not perfect. I&rsquo;m not all-knowing. But I have figured some stuff out that can help you. And the more I hang out with <a href=\"https:\/\/youtu.be\/Gfq0mFWmuzI\">people who are much more successful than I<\/a>, the more I realize that success is not an accident. It&rsquo;s not luck. A big part of getting ahead is the ability to focus while other people are distracted.<\/p>\n<p>So get focused now. Not in January.<\/p>\n<p><em>Right now.<\/em><\/p>\n<p><em>This <a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/252553\">article<\/a> originally appeared on <a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\">Entrepreneur.com<\/a><\/em><\/p>\n<p><em>More from Entrepreneur.com:<\/em><\/p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/241309\" target=\"_blank\">4 Ways to Banish Post-Holiday Blues From the Workplace<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/241289\" target=\"_blank\">Why You Don&#8217;t Keep Your Resolutions&#8230;And How to Fix That<\/a><\/li>\n<li><a href=\"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/241332\" target=\"_blank\">9 New Year&#8217;s Resolutions for Every Entrepreneur<\/a><\/li>\n<\/ul>\n","read_more":true,"section":{"name":"Ideas","slug":"ideas","url":"http:\/\/time.com\/ideas\/","description":"TIME Ideas hosts the world's leading voices, providing commentary and expertise on the most compelling events in news, society, and culture. Is How Successful People Get Ahead During the Holidays","description":"They live the '13-Month Year'","google_news":"success, career, new year, new years resolution, new year resolution, success Year'","canonical_link":"http:\/\/www.entrepreneur.com\/article\/252553"}},{"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/4133785\/donation-tech-leaders\/","shortlink":"http:\/\/ti.me\/1QUPrKv","title":"16 Tech Titans Who Plan to Donate Their Fortunes","friendly_title":"16 Tech Titans Who Plan to Donate Their Fortunes","post_type":"post","available":true,"time_article":true,"comments_allowed":true,"sub_learn_more_url":"https:\/\/subscription.time.com\/storefront\/subscribe-to-time\/link\/1032487.html","show_comments":true,"short_title":"16 Tech Titans Who Plan to Donate Their Fortunes","excerpt":"From Bill Gates to Sheryl Sandberg","format":"video","time":{"pretty":"Dec. 2, 2015","published":"2015-12-02 17:33:56","updated":"2015-12-02 22:33:56","minute":"5:33 pm","short":"12\/2"},"authors":[{"id":13176886,"url":"http:\/\/time.com\/author\/business-insider\/","name":"Madeline Stone, Biz Carson \/ Business Insider","bio":"","short_bio":"","types":["contributor"],"twitter":"businessinsider","twitter_url":"https:\/\/twitter.com\/businessinsider","gplus":"","fb":"","email":"","thumbnail":null,"contributor":true,"search_link":false}],"has_authors":true,"content":"<p>Some entrepreneurs who have made billions off of their tech ventures like to spend them in some pretty <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/vintage-silicon-valley-photos-2014-7\">extravagant ways<\/a>, whether it be on private planes, summer homes, or even an <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/richard-bransons-necker-island-reopens-2013-10\">entire island<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Others turn to more philanthropic efforts, choosing to donate their wealth to different causes through foundations and trusts.<\/p>\n<p>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/mark-zuckerberg-is-a-dad-has-a-girl-named-max-2015-12\">announced<\/a> the birth of his daughter Max on Tuesday afternoon.<\/p>\n<p>Along with the official announcement, he <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/mark-zuckerberg-giving-away-99-of-his-facebook-shares-2015-12\">shared<\/a> that he and wife Priscilla Chan plan to give away 99% of their Facebook shares &mdash; currently valued at about $45 billion &mdash; to charity.<\/p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve rounded up some of the other most generous people in tech, all of whom have decided to donate large portions of their wealth to charity rather than leave all of it to their children.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Microsoft co-founder Bill Gates<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Gates has been open about his decision not to leave his $84.9 billion fortune to his three children. They <a href=\"http:\/\/www.cnn.com\/2011\/TECH\/innovation\/06\/13\/personal.details.bill.gates.mashable\/index.html\">will reportedly inherit<\/a> just a small slice, about $10 million each.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I definitely think leaving kids massive amounts of money is not a favor to them,&#8221; <a href=\"http:\/\/www.thedailybeast.com\/articles\/2013\/02\/11\/bill-gates-answers-questions-in-reddit-ama.html\">he said<\/a> in a Reddit AMA.<\/p>\n<p>He founded the Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation in 1994, and it currently has more than $38 billion in assets. Gates also teamed up with longtime friend Warren Buffett to start a campaign called <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/index.html\">&#8220;The Giving Pledge,&#8221;<\/a> which encourages other billionaires to donate at least half of their fortune to charity.<\/p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper brightcove-size-large\" data-pos=\"11\" data-continuous=\"1\" data-playlist=\"0\"><object id=\"bc-video-3903524596001-11\" class=\"BrightcoveExperience\"><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#000000\"><param name=\"width\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"height\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"playerID\" value=\"1847503743001\"><param name=\"isVid\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"isUI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"dynamicStreaming\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"videoSmoothing\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"linkBaseURL\" value=\"http:\/\/ti.me\/1QUPrKv\"><param name=\"includeAPI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"templateLoadHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad\"><param name=\"templateReadyHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady\"><param name=\"wmode\" value=\"opaque\"><param name=\"htmlFallback\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"@videoPlayer\" value=\"3903524596001\"><\/object><\/div><\/div><\/p>\n<p><strong>AOL co-founder Steve Case<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Case helped millions of Americans get online, and now he&#8217;s donating much of his wealth to developing other technologies.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/www.insidephilanthropy.com\/guide-to-individual-donors\/steve-case.html\">He founded<\/a> the Case Foundation in 1997, which focuses on using technology to make philanthropy more effective. He also started an investment firm called Revolution, which invests in startups outside of Silicon Valley, and signed the Giving Pledge.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We share the view that those to whom much is given, much is expected. We realize we have been given a unique platform and opportunity, and we are committed to doing the best we can with it,&#8221; he and wife Jean <a href=\"http:\/\/www.reuters.com\/article\/2010\/12\/09\/us-wealth-philanthropy-billionaires-fact-idUSTRE6B81HM20101209\">wrote.<\/a>&#8220;We do not believe our assets are &#8216;ours&#8217; but rather we try to be the responsible stewards of these resources.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Salesforce CEO Marc Benioff<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Benioff recently launched a <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/benioff-tech-sector-needs-to-give-back-2014-3\">campaign called SF Gives<\/a>, which challenged tech companies to raise $10 million for San Francisco-based nonprofit programs in just 60 days.<\/p>\n<p>He&#8217;s encouraged other corporations to follow <a href=\"http:\/\/www.salesforcefoundation.org\/about-us\/sharethemodel\/\">his 1\/1\/1 model<\/a>, which says that a company should donate 1% of its equity, 1% of its employees&#8217; time, and 1% of its resources to philanthropic efforts.<\/p>\n<p>He and wife Lynne <a href=\"http:\/\/www.ucsf.edu\/news\/2014\/04\/113131\/ucsf-benioff-children%E2%80%99s-hospital-children%E2%80%99s-hospital-oakland-receive-100m-gift\">have also personally given<\/a> a total of $200 million to the children&#8217;s hospital at UCSF.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Qualcomm co-founder Irwin Jacobs<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Together with wife Joan, <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/profile\/irwin-jacobs\/\">Jacobs has given away some $500 million<\/a> of his fortune to charitable causes that include the Cornell Tech Roosevelt Island campus, MIT fellowships and the San Diego Symphony.<\/p>\n<p>He&#8217;s also signed the <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/\">Giving Pledge<\/a>, promising to give away at least half of the billions he made with the electronics firm he founded.<\/p>\n<p><strong>eBay founder Pierre Omidyar<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Omidyar and his wife Pam are some of the most generous people in tech, having given away <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/the-most-and-least-generous-people-in-tech-2014-3\">more than $1 billion<\/a> of the vast fortune they made when eBay went public in 1998.<\/p>\n<p>They signed the <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/index.html\">Giving Pledge<\/a> in 2010. Forbes <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/profile\/pierre-omidyar\/\">estimates<\/a> Omidyar&#8217;s net worth at $8.1 billion.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;In 2001, I publicly stated that we intend to give away the vast majority of our wealth during our lifetime,&#8221; the couple <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/\">said in their pledge letter<\/a>. &#8220;Our view is fairly simple. We have more money than our family will ever need. There&#8217;s no need to hold onto it when it can be put to use today, to help solve some of the world&#8217;s most intractable problems.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>They&#8217;ve also donated eBay shares to the Omidyar Network, their philanthropic investment firm, and are the single biggest private donors in the fight against human trafficking.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Intel co-founder Gordon Moore<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Moore has <a href=\"http:\/\/www.insidephilanthropy.com\/guide-to-individual-donors\/gordon-moore.html\">given away more than $1 billion<\/a> to charitable causes, donating about half of his wealth to create the Moore Foundation in 2001.<\/p>\n<p>The foundation, which focuses on issues of environmental conservation, health measures, and the San Francisco community, currently <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/profile\/gordon-moore\/\">has more than $5 billion in assets<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>He and wife Betty signed Gates&#8217; Giving Pledge in 2012.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are pleased to be a part of the Giving Pledge not only because we are able to commit these funds, but because we believe they can lead to real learning and measurable change,&#8221; <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/\">they said.<\/a><\/p>\n<p><strong>Tesla CEO Elon Musk<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Musk may have five young boys from his first marriage &mdash; one set of twins and one set of triplets &mdash; but <a href=\"http:\/\/www.insidephilanthropy.com\/guide-to-individual-donors\/elon-musk.html\">he&#8217;s already donated<\/a> much of his $12.9 billion fortune to renewable energy, science and engineering education, and pediatric health.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/2012-04-19\/buffett-joined-by-12-families-pledging-most-wealth-to-charity.html\">He signed<\/a> the Giving Pledge in 2012, committing to donate the majority of his wealth to charitable causes. He <a href=\"http:\/\/www.reuters.com\/article\/2014\/04\/25\/us-tesla-executives-musk-idUSBREA3O1OY20140425\">receives only $1 a year<\/a> for his work with Tesla.<\/p>\n<div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper brightcove-size-large\" data-pos=\"12\" data-continuous=\"1\" data-playlist=\"0\"><object id=\"bc-video-110961589001-12\" class=\"BrightcoveExperience\"><param name=\"bgcolor\" value=\"#000000\"><param name=\"width\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"height\" value=\"100%\"><param name=\"playerID\" value=\"1847503743001\"><param name=\"isVid\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"isUI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"dynamicStreaming\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"videoSmoothing\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"linkBaseURL\" value=\"http:\/\/ti.me\/1QUPrKv\"><param name=\"includeAPI\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"templateLoadHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateLoad\"><param name=\"templateReadyHandler\" value=\"Time.application.brightcoveFacade._onTemplateReady\"><param name=\"wmode\" value=\"opaque\"><param name=\"htmlFallback\" value=\"true\"><param name=\"@videoPlayer\" value=\"110961589001\"><\/object><\/div><\/div>\n<p><strong>Google CEO Larry Page<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Page, on the other hand, has a somewhat unique idea for what he would like to happen to his wealth.<\/p>\n<p>He once told Charlie Rose that instead of giving his billions to his two children, he would rather give it to entrepreneurs like Elon Musk, who are coming up with big ideas to change the world.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;[Musk] wants to go to Mars. That&#8217;s a worthy goal,&#8221; <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/larry-page-elon-musk-2014-3\">he said<\/a>. &#8220;We have a lot of employees at Google who&#8217;ve become pretty wealthy. You&#8217;re working because you want to change the world and make it better; if the company you work for is worthy of your time, why not your money as well? We just don&#8217;t think about that. I&#8217;d like for us to help out more than we are.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"content-ad\" id=\"content-ad-4133785\"><\/div>\n<p><strong>Spanx CEO Sara Blakely<\/strong><\/p>\n<div class=\"slide-module clearfix\">\n<div class=\"slide-content\">\n<p>Sara Blakely, CEO of Spanx, became the first woman to <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/clareoconnor\/2013\/05\/07\/spanx-mogul-sara-blakely-becomes-first-female-billionaire-to-join-gates-buffett-giving-pledge\/\">sign the Giving Pledge in 2013<\/a> and commit to donating the majority of her wealth to charities specifically aimed at women.<\/p>\n<p>When she told her then 3-year-old son that she was going to give away half her money, he reportedly <a href=\"http:\/\/www.dailymail.co.uk\/femail\/article-2322201\/Billionaire-Spanx-founder-Sara-Blakely-donate-half-fortune-charity-woman-join-Warren-Buffett-Bill-Gates-Giving-Pledge.html\">said<\/a>, &#8220;OK, Mommy, can we do a puzzle now?&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I pledge to invest in women because I believe it offers one of the greatest returns on investment. I am committed to the belief that we would all be in a much better place if half the human race (women) were empowered to prosper, invent, be educated, start their own businesses, run for office &mdash; essentially be given the chance to soar!&#8221; <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Blakely_Letter.pdf\">her letter said<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Oracle founder Larry Ellison<\/strong><\/p>\n<\/div>\n<\/div>\n<div class=\"slide-module clearfix\">\n<p>Even with his <a href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/life-of-larry-ellison-2014-9?op=1\">lavish lifestyle<\/a>, Larry Ellison has committed to <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Ellison_Letter.pdf\">giving away 95% of his wealth<\/a> to charitable causes, especially to <a href=\"http:\/\/www.ellisonfoundation.org\/\">his medical foundation<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Warren Buffett personally asked me to write this letter because he said I would be &#8216;setting an example&#8217; and &#8216;influencing others&#8217; to give. I hope he&#8217;s right,&#8221; his <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Ellison_Letter.pdf\">letter to the Giving Pledge<\/a> said in August 2010.<\/p>\n<p>Despite committing the majority of his wealth to charity, he also gave his children Oracle stock when they were still babies &mdash; and the company was also young. Now that the stock and company are worth a lot more, he <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/deborahljacobs\/2013\/06\/05\/larry-ellisons-trust-fund-babies\/\">reportedly<\/a> wants to teach them charitable giving, too.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Microsoft co-founder Paul Allen<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>While Paul Allen doesn&#8217;t have any direct descendants, his family is actively involved in his philanthropy.<\/p>\n<p>The Microsoft cofounder <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Allen_Letter.pdf\">signed the Giving Pledge in 2010<\/a> and plans to give the majority of his $17.2 billion estate to his <a href=\"http:\/\/www.pgafamilyfoundation.org\/\">Paul G. Allen Family Foundation<\/a>, which he runs with his sister Jody Allen, and to the other charitable work he&#8217;s involved in, like the <a href=\"http:\/\/allenai.org\/\">Allen Institute for Artificial Intelligence<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I&#8217;ve planned for many years now that the majority of my estate will be left to continue the work of the Foundation and to fund non-profit scientific research, like the ground breaking work being done at the Allen Institute for Brain Science,&#8221; he said in his Giving Pledge letter.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Asana CEO Dustin Moskovitz<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Facebook&#8217;s third employee, Dustin Moskovitz, is one of the youngest self-made billionaires to have signed the Giving Pledge.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;As a result of Facebook&#8217;s success, I&#8217;ve earned financial capital beyond my wildest expectations. Today, I view that reward not as personal wealth, but as a tool with which I hope to bring even more benefit to the world,&#8221; he <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Moskovitz_Tuna_Letter.pdf\">said in his letter<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Moskovitz and his partner, former Wall Street Journal reporter Cari Tuna, established <a href=\"http:\/\/www.goodventures.org\/about-us\">Good Ventures<\/a> as a philanthropic foundation to help distribute his wealth. Moskovitz is also now founder and CEO of <a href=\"https:\/\/asana.com\/\">Asana<\/a>, a collaboration software company.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Sheryl Sandberg, along with her late husband Dave Goldberg, <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/sites\/randalllane\/2014\/05\/09\/exclusive-sheryl-sandberg-pledges-to-give-away-half-her-fortune\/\">signed the Giving Pledge<\/a> in 2014 to give away half of her wealth. While the couple didn&#8217;t specify a cause, we have a feeling Sandberg&#8217;s book &#8220;Lean In&#8221; might be a pretty strong indication of where their money ends up.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Virgin Group founder Richard Branson<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Richard Branson&#8217;s children are philanthropists in their own right. Their son Sam set up a production company, Sundog Pictures, and their daughter Holly is involved in Big Change Charitable Trust, <a href=\"http:\/\/givingpledge.org\/pdf\/pledge-letters\/Branson_Letter.pdf\">according to their 2013 Giving Pledge letter<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The Virgin Group founder and his wife, Joan, signed the Giving Pledge in 2013 to give away half their wealth after they realized after several house fires that money does not lead to happiness.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Stuff really is not what brings happiness. Family, friends, good health and the satisfaction that comes from making a positive difference are what really matters,&#8221; Branson said in the announcement.<\/p>\n<p><strong>Netflix founder Reed Hastings<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>Netflix founder and CEO Reed Hastings and his wife, Patti Quillin, signed the Giving Pledge in 2012, when his net worth was valued only at $280 million. A new entrant on Forbes&#8217; World&#8217;s Billionaires list, Hastings now has a <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/profile\/reed-hastings-1\/\">net worth<\/a> of at least $1.6 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Hastings has an interest in education after he served as president of the California Board of Education from 2000 to 2004. The press release announcing their Giving Pledge hinted that it that might be where they put some of their money, since they &#8220;are active in educational philanthropy and politics with a specific focus on charter schools.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><strong>Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg<\/strong><\/p>\n<p>When Mark Zuckerberg signed the Giving Pledge in 2010, he was <a href=\"http:\/\/www.cbsnews.com\/news\/mark-zuckerberg-pledges-most-of-6-billion-fortune-to-charity\/\">only worth $6 billion<\/a>. Now his net worth is <a href=\"http:\/\/www.forbes.com\/profile\/mark-zuckerberg\/\">estimated<\/a> at $46.8 billion.<\/p>\n<p>Zuckerberg announced the birth of his daughter Max on December 1. In a Facebook <a href=\"https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/notes\/mark-zuckerberg\/a-letter-to-our-daughter\/10153375081581634\">post<\/a> announcing her arrival, Zuckerberg shared that he and wife Priscilla Chan plan to give away most of their wealth, rather than pass it on to Max.<\/p>\n<p>He shared the news in a letter addressed to his newborn daughter: &#8220;As you begin the next generation of the Chan Zuckerberg family, we also begin the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.facebook.com\/chanzuckerberginitiative\/\">Chan Zuckerberg Initiative<\/a> to join people across the world to advance human potential and promote equality for all children in the next generation. Our initial areas of focus will be personalized learning, curing disease, connecting people and building strong communities. We will give 99% of our Facebook shares &mdash; currently about $45 billion &mdash; during our lives to advance this mission. We know this is a small contribution compared to all the resources and talents of those already working on these issues. But we want to do what we can, working alongside many others.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The couple <a href=\"http:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/id\/102404197\">gave $75 million<\/a> in February 2015 to the San Francisco General Hospital, allowing it to add two trauma rooms and three operating rooms and to double the size of its emergency room.<\/p>\n<div class=\"article-video\"><div class=\"video-wrapper
